./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<section id="hp-storevirtual-dep-platform"> <title>HPE StoreVirtual Deployment Models supported in HPE Helion OpenStack</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>The following diagram displays the different development platforms supported in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>There are three supported models for deploying StoreVirtual in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>You can deploy and configure dedicated HPE StoreVirtual VSA Storage nodes using the HPE Helion OpenStack TripleO/Heat-based Installer. Licenses for these VSA nodes are included for use from HPE Helion OpenStack Compute Cloud Nodes only.</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>User deploys and configures StoreVirtual VSA in VMware ESX platform, and maps these to Cinder backends. Licenses for these must be separately procured and are not included with HPE Helion OpenStack</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>User installs StoreVirtual P4000 devices rather than using StoreVirtual VSA. These devices must be separately procured and are not included with HPE Helion OpenStack</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>Cinder is the block-based storage component of the HPE  Helion OpenStack platform for cloud computing. It facilitates the provisioning of storage in the form of block devices known as Cinder volumes. In the most common scenario, the Cinder volumes provide persistent storage to guest virtual machines (known as instances) that are managed by OpenStack Compute software. Cinder is based on the distributed architecture which can scale horizontally and serve concurrent volume management requests.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses StoreVirtual as a backend to Cinder to realize horizontally scalable block storage. StoreVirtual is unique in the sense that storage controller runs as a virtual appliance and helps realize Software Defined Block Storage.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>Differentiated storage offerings based on performance and quality can be realized in HPE Helion OpenStack by creating clusters of different capabilities, configuring clusters as backends and mapping these backends to different volume types as suggested above.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>This document provides guidance on configuring your HPE Helion OpenStack network securely</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack has many built-in security controls, but the customer must take responsibility for configuring the network devices that integrate Helion services into an existing data center environment.  This includes defining firewall rules at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against external abuse) as well as defining router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors).</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is deployed on three physical networks: IPMI, Fibre Channel, and the Cloud LAN which is subdivided into VLANs to produce the External, Management, and Service LANs as depicted in <xref type="section" href="#topic19933/fig1">Figure 1</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<section id="fig1"> <title>Figure 1: Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>In <xref type="section" href="#topic19933/fig1">Figure 1</xref>, the Border Router and the Aggregation Router are customer devices that perform routing at the perimeter of the environment. The Load Balancer is a recommended customer device to provide TLS termination. The following sections provide guidance on how to configure these network devices for improved security.  Note that HPE Helion OpenStack includes IPtable rules on each node to close network ports that are not needed, but applying additional rules to your network devices (as indicated in the sections that follow) will provide increased security.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>As shown in figure <xref type="section" href="#topic19933/fig1">Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</xref>, all of the Cloud Controller servers are members of all three VLANs. However, these servers have IP addresses configured only for the management VLAN.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>To protect against external attacks on Helion services, your firewall should be configured with a rule to block any requests originating from outside the network that attempts to reach any of the HPE Helion OpenStack nodes or any 3PAR StoreServ  or StoreVirtual VSA appliances dedicated to the HPE Helion OpenStack installation, other than those indicated this table:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>The customer deploying HPE Helion OpenStack is responsible for securing the block storage networks. Network data flows for block storage should be restricted using access control lists or other mechanisms in the customer's network devices which can include routers, switches, or firewalls. Block storage data flows interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack are described here to assist with defining those controls. References are given to documentation on data flows within the storage cluster itself, but not necessarily interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack nodes.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports StoreVirtual or 3Par StoreServ storage arrays which are described separately.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion Openstack supports iSCSI or Fibre Channel connectivity with 3PAR StoreServ. If using Fibre Channel, then the Compute nodes and the overcloud controller hosting Block Storage (Cinder) will require Fibre Channel connectivity with the 3PAR array. For iSCSI, connectivity will be through the management VLAN. The StoreServ REST API and SSH command line interfaces must be accessible from the management VLAN as well.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>If your deployment includes ESX Integration, you can improve network security by configuring access control lists for the ESX network.  The ESX Tenant network (also shown below) is managed by the Networking Operations service (Neutron).  The ESX network is not installed or managed by HPE Helion OpenStack You must install and manage this network and makes sure there is a route to the Management network.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic19933/fig9">Figure 9</xref> depicts the following Logical deployment of the ESX Integration in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack by
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="features-in-hp-helion-openstack-101"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.01</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Security documentation</b> - A new document is included in this release that contains recommendations for securing your HPE Helion OpenStack network. <xref href="1.0commercial.install-GA-security.dita" >Configuring your network securely</xref> details the firewall rules you can apply at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against external abuse and defines router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</b> The <xref href="1.0commerical.flexible-control-pane-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</xref> introduces the capacity to deploy the control plane in a virtual environment in addition to the current baremetal physical deployment. This new configuration reduces the control plane footprint to just three servers from the current seven to ten servers.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="features-in-hp-helion-openstack-10"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.0</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>OpenStack Services</b> - The full set of standard <xref href="1.0commerical.services-overview.dita">Open Stack services"</xref> is in HPE Helion OpenStack Nova (Compute), Swift (Object Operations), Cinder (Volume Operations), Neutron (Networking Operations), Glance (Image Operations), Keystone (Identity Management), Horizon (Helion dashboard), Heat (Orchestration), TripleO, and Ironic.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Support for VMWare ESX</b> - VMWare ESX is a baremetal hypervisor. HPE Helion OpenStack makes ESX host onboarding and management easier and lets you setup the ESX proxy node during installation of the overcloud.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>This page introduces you to HPE Helion OpenStack an enterprise-grade distribution of the OpenStack cloud operating system.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack allows you to easily deploy OpenStack Cloud Services in a secure, highly available configuration, and subsequently deploy, manage and operate your cloud infrastructure in production.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic25331/Helion-services">HPE Helion OpenStack services</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<section id="Helion-services"> <title>HPE Helion OpenStack Services- Functional Overview</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>The following table outlines the functionality of HPE Helion OpenStack services based on the type of users - Users and Administrators. For a complete description of these services, see the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-overview.dita" >Services Overview</xref> page.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Compute supports an API to instantiate and manage virtual servers on KVM  and VMware ESX hypervisors. <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--> Users can create and manage the life cycle of virtual machines (suspend, resume, snapshot, and so forth), attach block storage volumes, work with security groups and key pairs, and associate floating IP addresses. <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-compute-overview.dita" >Learn more</xref> about the Compute Operations service.</entry>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Block Storage supports an API to instantiate and manage block storage volumes on HPE StoreServ 3PAR devices and StoreVirtual Software Defined Storage. <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->User can create volumes, attach them to VMs, and take snapshots and backups.
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Object and Operations service helps manage the storage and retrieval of objects in publicly accessible physical machines. 
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Network Operations service provides network connectivity and IP addressing for virtual machines managed by Compute service.<!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--> User can create and configure virtual networks and routers, subnets, floating IP addresses, security groups, load balancers and firewalls.<!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-networking-overview.dita" >Learn more</xref> about the Network Operations service.</entry>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Identity Operations service provides one-stop authentication.
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Image Operations service helps to manage virtual machine images, including querying and updating image metadata, and retrieval of the actual image data.
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>Administrators can download content such as software patches and updates from the HPE Helion CODN and apply the downloaded content to their Helion OpenStack installation. </entry>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>The HPE Helion OpenStack Sirius service is a REST-based web service for storage device management. It is used to configure of storage services such as the  Block Storage and the Object Operations services that run in the overcloud and manage various storage devices.
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:     <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><xref href="1.0commerical.services-sirius-overview.dita" >Learn more</xref> HPE Helion OpenStack Sirius service.</entry> 
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:    <entry>HPE Helion OpenStack Distributed Virtual Routing (DVR) allows you to define connectivity among different Virtual Network Switches (VNS) as well as connectivity between VNS hosts and the external network. HPE Helion OpenStack provides Distributed Virtual Routing to cloud users.
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:        <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--><xref href="1.0commerical.services-dvr-overview.dita" >Learn more</xref> HPE Helion OpenStack DVR service.</entry> 
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>You can deploy HPE Helion OpenStack in two different environments depending on the hypervisor: KVM or ESX.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>The following hardware requirements are required to install HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses three linked installation phases, called OpenStack-on-OpenStack (TripleO), to deploy a complete OpenStack cloud. TripleO simulates the deployment of OpenStack by creating and configuring baremetal servers to successfully run a cloud deployment.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-tripleo-overview.dita:<p>The <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.install-GA-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack installation</xref> follows the standard TripleO deployment model, creating a seed, an undercloud and an overcloud.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-tripleo-overview.dita:<b>seed</b> - The seed cloud is a bootable image that is deployed in a VM instance. This image, which is provided as part of HPE Helion OpenStack contains the minimum services required for OpenStack to function and to provision physical hardware to deploy the undercloud.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-tripleo-overview.dita:<p>For more information on the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment model, see <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Technical Overview</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack Block Storage Volume Operations uses the OpenStack Cinder (Block Storage) service to manage storage volumes, including creating volumes, creating volume snapshots, and configuring volumes.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses StoreVirtual as a backend to Cinder to realize horizontally scalable block storage. StoreVirtual is unique in the sense that the storage controller runs as a virtual appliance and helps realize Software Defined Block Storage. To use StoreVirtual you must use the KVM hypervisor.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack also supports HPE StoreServ 3PAR as a Cinder backend.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>You can use the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.0commercial.dashboard.how-works.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Dashboard</xref> to work with the Volume Operations service.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:The following lists of tasks can be performed by a user or administrator through the [HPE Helion OpenStack Dashboard](/helion/openstack/dashboard/how-works/), the [API](http://developer.openstack.org/api-ref-blockstorage-v2.html) or [CLI](http://docs.openstack.org/cli-reference/content/cinderclient_commands.html).
./commercial/GA1/1.0commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>For more general information on how to operate your cloud, refer to the <xref href="http://docs.openstack.org/ops/" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack Operations Guide</xref>. The <i>Architecture</i> section contains useful information about how an OpenStack Cloud is put together. However, the HPE Helion OpenStack takes care of these details for you. The <i>Operations</i> section contains information on how to manage the system.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:<p>Welcome to the HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1 update instructions. These instructions apply to existing HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1 installations and describe how you can update your HPE Helion OpenStack cloud environment from v1.1 to v1.1.1. (The process of updating a HPE Helion OpenStack v1.0 or v1.01 release to HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1 is not supported.)</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:The HPE Helion Development Platform requires HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1. However, HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1 does not currently support updating the HPE Helion Development Platform from v1.1 to v1.2.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:**Note for Helion Development Platform version v1.1 users**: This Helion OpenStack version v1.1.1 update procedure supports Helion Development Platform version v1.2, (and only Helion Development Platform version v1.2). For users who have installed Helion OpenStack v1.1 and Helion Development Platform v1.1, when you update to HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1, you also need to update to Helion Development Platform v1.2.  
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:**Important for HPE Helion Development Platform users**: During the HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1.1 update, you will need to stop your Helion Development Platform services. Failure to do so will likely damage your existing Helion Development Platform v1.1 installation.

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:            HPE Helion OpenStack overcloud is now updated.</p></li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita:This procedure allows you to update your overcloud installation from HPE Helion OpenStack v1.1 to Helion v1.1.1 by executing the update commands directly and not relying on the update scripts. (HPE Helion Development Platform users must shutdown before updating the overcloud. When the update is complete, the Development Platform VMs need to be restarted.)

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>Thank you for your interest in HPE Helion OpenStack This document provides an overview of the features contained within HPE Helion OpenStack version 1.1.1, including known issues and workarounds, and where to find further information on the product release:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic18834/features">Features in HPE Helion OpenStack</xref> </li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="features"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack by release.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic18834/111">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1.1</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic18834/110">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic18834/101">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.01</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic18834/10">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.0</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="111"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1.1</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:HPE Helion OpenStack through its centralized logging infrastructure (Logstash,) can be configured to send events and logs to an HPE ArcSight endpoint. The HPE ArcSight connector can, in turn, be configured to receive logs and events in real time from this Logstash configuration inside an HPE Helion OpenStack environment.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>Integration with HPE ArcSight provides the ability to monitor, analyze, and correlate HPE Helion OpenStack logs through HPE ArcSight Logger and ESM and supports continuous security monitoring of the entire HPE Helion OpenStack infrastructure. Technical details of this integration along with a step-by-step tutorial are available in the whitepaper entitled <xref href="http://www8.hp.com/h20195/V2/GetDocument.aspx?docname=4AA5-8025ENW&amp;cc=us&amp;lc=en" scope="external" format="html" >Monitoring HPE Helion OpenStack with HPE ArcSight</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="110"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>OpenStack Juno support</b> All of the <xref href="1.1commerical.services-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack services</xref> have been updated to <xref href="http://www.openstack.org/software/juno/" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack Juno</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Metering services</b> The <xref href="1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Telemetry and Reporting service</xref> leverages the OpenStack Ceilometer metering service. The Metering Operations service takes specified measurements of both physical and virtual resources, including physical servers and network devices such as switches and firewalls.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Windows Server validation as a guest O/S on KVM</b> - HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1 has achieved <xref href="http://www.windowsservercatalog.com/svvp/" scope="external" format="html" >Microsoft Server Virtualization Validation Program</xref> (SVVP) approval.  As such, HPE Helion OpenStack is a validated and supported virtual environment for Windows Server 2012 R2, 2012, 2008 R2, and 2008.  <!--HPM-29--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>For information on creating and deploying a Microsoft Windows Server that is Microsoft SVVP compliant on HPE Helion OpenStack as a Nova compute VM, see <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.create-deploy-certified-microsoft-windows-guest-image.dita" >How to build a Microsoft Windows Server guest image for HPE Helion OpenStack</xref>.  <!--DOCS-917--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>New Horizon Dashboard functionality</b> - The <xref href="1.1commercial.install-GA-DNSaaS.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack DNSaaS service</xref> functionality is now accessible through the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-horizon-overview.dita" >Horizon dashboard</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Transport Layer Security (TLS) support</b> - HPE Helion OpenStack now supports TLS protocols to protect internal traffic for Overcloud OpenStack API and endpoints. <!--HPM16--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Identity service</b> - The Identity service, based on OpenStack Keystone V2 or V3 provides one-stop authentication, including Identity, Token, Catalog and Policy services. See <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-identity-overview.dita" >Identity Service Overview</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:  <b>Compute Service Configuration Drive</b> - The HPE Helion OpenStack compute service can be configured to <xref href="http://docs.openstack.org/user-guide/cli_config_drive.html" scope="external" format="html"> write metadata to a special configuration drive</xref> that contains information normally available through the metadata service.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Security documentation</b> - A new document is included in this release that contains recommendations for securing your HPE Helion OpenStack network. <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita" >Configuring your network securely</xref> details the firewall rules you can apply at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against external abuse and defines router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</b> - The <xref href="1.1commerical.flexible-control-pane-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</xref> introduces the capacity to deploy the control plane in a virtual environment in addition to the current baremetal physical deployment. This new configuration reduces the control plane footprint to just three servers from the current seven to ten servers.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commerical.services-customer-provided-certificates.dita:<p>In HPE Helion OpenStack all services are configured to use transport layer security (TLS) as their communication protocol. Since TLS is secure (HTTPS), it checks for a certificate from a certificate authority (CA).</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commerical.services-customer-provided-certificates.dita:<p>Following this procedure will configure HPE Helion OpenStack to use customer-provided certificates for all endpoints. It will explain how to configure the existing load balancer to terminate SSL connections with a client provided server certificate and re-encrypt traffic to the service back ends served by stunnel proxies. Here you will also add the client-provided trust chain to the ECA trust file. Note that while this eliminates the need to reconfigure serices to use the certificate you as the customer provide, services may need to be restarted.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commerical.services-customer-provided-certificates.dita:  <li>   Restart all HPE Helion OpenStack services on all nodes.
./commercial/GA1/1.1.1commerical.services-customer-provided-certificates.dita:<p>The services use the endpoints to talk to other services and they'll fail validation because they're designed to find the ECA certificate in a specific file location. They also need to be told to trust the client provided server certificate. Because the cacert location has been hard coded in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1.1,  the suggested solution is to put both public CA-signed certtificates and internal CA-signed certificates in a single file.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<othermeta name="product-version" content="HPE Helion Openstack"/>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<othermeta name="product-version1" content="HPE Helion Openstack"/>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<p>The Transport Layer Security (TLS) protocol, successor of SSL, provides the mechanisms to ensure authentication, non-repudiation, confidentiality, and integrity of user communications to the HPE Helion OpenStack services and between the HPE Helion OpenStack services themselves.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<p>The TLS connections are facilitated by providing each node with a signed certificate from an internal certificate authority server (Ephemeral CA server) that is built into HPE Helion OpenStack and installed on the Overcloud Controller nodes. These certificates are regenerated frequently - typically at least every 12 hours. The Helion Ephemeral certificate authority (CA) server uses a private key to sign these certificates provided to the OpenStack services, and an associated public certificate can be used to validate these newly signed certs. This key/cert pair can either be generated at installation time or be provided by the installer as an input to the installation process.  If you would like to use certificates from your own CA, please see <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1.1commerical.services-customer-provided-certificates.dita">Configuring support for customer-provided certificates</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<p>If the deployer has not provided a key/cert pair, the self-signed certificate created during the installation process must be retrieved from the seed at /root/eca.crt after deployment. This certificate can then be used to authenticate the TLS connection when connecting to any of the overcloud OpenStack services in the HPE Helion OpenStack cloud. This can be retrieved using the following command:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commcerical.install-TLS.dita:<p>If a self-signed certificate was created during the HPE Helion OpenStack installation, you must install the generated certificate in your browser as a trusted CA to prevent messages about insecure connections when connecting to the Horizon IP address. This can be done by importing the eca.crt file from the seed VM as a trusted CA into your browser software.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack bundles and facilitates deployment of HPE StoreVirtual VSA which can be configured as backend for OpenStack Cinder Block Storage.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports multiple clusters. For minimal deployment, you can create a management group with one cluster and with a single StoreVirtual node on it.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>HPE StoreVirtual VSA enables the following features in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<section id="hp-storevirtual-dep-platform"> <title>HPE StoreVirtual Deployment Models supported in HPE Helion OpenStack</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>The following diagram displays the different development platforms supported in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>There are three supported models for deploying StoreVirtual in HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>You can deploy and configure dedicated HPE StoreVirtual VSA Storage nodes using the HPE Helion OpenStack TripleO/Heat-based Installer. Licenses for these VSA nodes are included for use from HPE Helion OpenStack Compute Cloud Nodes only.</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>User deploys and configures StoreVirtual VSA in VMware ESX platform, and maps these to Cinder backends. Licenses for these must be separately procured and are not included with HPE Helion OpenStack</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<li>User installs StoreVirtual P4000 devices rather than using StoreVirtual VSA. These devices must be separately procured and are not included with HPE Helion OpenStack</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>Cinder is the block-based storage component of the HPE  Helion OpenStack platform for cloud computing. It facilitates the provisioning of storage in the form of block devices known as Cinder volumes. In the most common scenario, the Cinder volumes provide persistent storage to guest virtual machines (known as instances) that are managed by OpenStack Compute software. Cinder is based on the distributed architecture which can scale horizontally and serve concurrent volume management requests.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses StoreVirtual as a backend to Cinder to realize horizontally scalable block storage. StoreVirtual is unique in the sense that storage controller runs as a virtual appliance and helps realize Software Defined Block Storage.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.-vsa-overview.dita:<p>Differentiated storage offerings based on performance and quality can be realized in HPE Helion OpenStack by creating clusters of different capabilities, configuring clusters as backends and mapping these backends to different volume types as suggested above.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<section id="what-is-hp-helion-openstack"> <title>What is HPE Helion OpenStack<!--Removed anchor point whatHelion--><!-- id="whatHelion" --></title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is a commercial distribution built on OpenStack technology that provides an open, scalable, highly available enterprise-grade cloud software platform to help customers build, manage, and consume hybrid clouds.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<!-- Removed per Gary's comments I HPE Helion OpenStack is the first OpenStack distribution from HP. It is free to download and will be kept updated frequently to stay current with OpenStack developments. It is the foundational technology for all HPE Helion products in the future.-->
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<section id="what-does-hp-helion-openstack-enable-me-to-do"> <title>What does HPE Helion OpenStack enable me to do?<!--Removed anchor point distroenable--><!-- id="distroenable" --></title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<!-- #### Removed per Gary's comments I How does HPE Helion OpenStack compare to other OpenStack distributions on the market? #### {#howcompare}
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:HPE Helion OpenStack is one of the first distributions in the market, based on up-to-date code from the OpenStack community. It is derived from pure OpenStack and open source technologies, configured and packaged by HP. For example, TripleO, which is used for installation and update, is the official OpenStack project for deployment.-->
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>A seed VM is a bootable KVM VM image provided as part of HPE Helion OpenStack and is deployed in a VM instance. This image contains the minimum services required of OpenStack to function and to be able to provision physical hardware to deploy the undercloud. The services are Nova, Neutron, Glance, Keystone, Ironic &amp; Heat.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>This is the first phase of the HPE Helion OpenStack installation.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>This is the second phase of the HPE Helion OpenStack installation.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>Setting up the overcloud completes the overall HPE Helion OpenStack installation process.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:On June 30th, we announced a preview of HPE Helion OpenStack that enables you to deploy an OpenStack TripleO-based cloud experience and evaluate the Icehouse release of OpenStack  
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<section id="does-hp-helion-openstack-work-with-hybrid-or-public-cloud-projects"> <title>Does HPE Helion OpenStack work with hybrid or public cloud projects?<!--Removed anchor point hybridorpubliccloud--><!-- id="hybridorpubliccloud" --></title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.faq.dita:<p>No. Currently, HPE Helion OpenStack is supported by HPE for small-scale, private cloud deployments only.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-apparmor.dita:<p>AppArmor profiles can modified, as needed, for your organization. However, the default profiles, as installed, have been configured to provide optimal protection for HPE Helion OpenStack All profiles are configured for <i>enforce</i> mode (for more information, see <xref type="section" href="#topic2805/modes">AppArmor profile modes</xref> below) and designed to mitigate hostile VMs exploiting hypervisor breakout attacks.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-apparmor.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack follows the <xref href="http://wiki.apparmor.net/index.php/Libvirt" scope="external" format="html" >svirt model</xref> to provide guest isolation. Every guest VM is locked down to be able to access only its own configuration files, disk files and volume devices.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<searchtitle>HPE Helion Openstack 1.1: Editing the Installation Configuration JSON File</searchtitle>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<othermeta name="product-version" content="HPE Helion Openstack 1.1"/>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<othermeta name="product-version1" content="HPE Helion Openstack 1.1"/>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<p>(If you already have 1.1 installed, you can update Helion OpenStack from 1.1 to 1.1.1 by following the update procedures described in <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1.1commercial.helion-update.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1.1 Update Guide</xref>.)</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack Installation process requires various configuration parameters to be specified. This is achieved through environment variables.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<p>A user who is installing HPE Helion OpenStack can enter all required environment variables using a JSON (JavaScript Object Notation) file that comes with the installation package.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<codeph>esx-custom-ips.json</codeph> - Use this file for installing HPE Helion OpenStack with ESX hypervisor support.</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<codeph>esx-custom-ips-vlan.json</codeph> - Use this file for installing HPE Helion OpenStack with ESX hypervisor support with a VLAN provider network.</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<codeph>kvm-custom-ips.json</codeph> - Use this file for installing HPE Helion OpenStack with KVM hypervisor support.</li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:  <xref href="1.1commercial.install-GA-prereqs.dita#topic9786/csv">Return to HPE Helion OpenStack Installation Prerequisites</xref></li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<codeph>control_virtual_router_id</codeph> - Use this variable to set a unique idenitifier for the HPE Helion OpenStack installation.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses keepalived to manage virtual IPs. keepalived uses a unique id to synchronise its activities. If you plan to run multiple installations of HPE Helion OpenStack on the same network, each installation must be configured with a unique id by setting the environment variable <codeph>control_virtual_router_id</codeph> to a unique number (from 0 to 255) before running the installation. The default value, if unset, is 51.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<codeph>cloud_type</codeph> - Use this variable to specify whether the HPE Helion OpenStack will be installed with KVM or ESX hypervisor support.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-JSON.dita:<p>Helion OpenStack requires a third VLAN network called as Service Network which connects trusted VMs in overcloud to communicate with cloud infrastructure components in undercloud. The purpose is to aggregate logs of PaaS components running on the VMs in the overcloud to the undercloud via this network.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-NTP.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses stratum 10. Using a numerically high stratum ensures that this is only used if all external clocks fail. This will mitigate skew until external clocks return to service.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is designed to deliver an open source OpenStack solution at the modest scale. A baremetal multi-node deployment consists of a minimum of 8 baremetal servers, to which you can add up to 100 Compute nodes:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses three linked installation phases, called <xref href="https://wiki.openstack.org/wiki/TripleO" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack-on-OpenStack (TripleO) deployment model</xref> to deploy a complete OpenStack cloud.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is provided with two baremetal installation options depending on your system configuration.  It allows you to manage the KVM and ESX hypervisors and provision virtual machines.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports VMWare ESX hypervisor. With our ESX integration, you can provision and manage an overcloud ESX cluster. VMWare vCenter Compute driver is used as a part of ESX integration. The VMware vCenter driver connects to ESX clusters in a vCenter through Compute proxy nodes. A Compute node scheduler sees each cluster as compute and uses the same for scheduling a new instances.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Virtual Cloud Networking (VCN) application is an enhanced Networking Operations (Neutron) module of HPE Helion OpenStack that delivers network virtualization to orchestrate your data center infrastructure.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>This section introduces the overall process you will follow to install HPE Helion OpenStack Information or links to information will be provided at the time it is needed.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>You install HPE Helion OpenStack by first installing the seed cloud by running a single command. The host system for the seed cloud is called the seed cloud host.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>The key to a smooth installation of HPE Helion OpenStack is planning.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>After HPE Helion OpenStack is installed and you have verified that the undercloud and overcloud nodes are up and running, there are a number of configurations that you need to consider, including incorporating DNS as a Service (DNSaaS), storage methods, and other considerations based on your environment.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<p>Users and client software must be able to verify the TLS certificates used on the Helion APIs and web interface, so the deployer must make the CA certificate available to users. ./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-overview.dita:<b>Important:</b> When installing HPE Helion OpenStack it is your responsibility to track the physical location (slot number and rack) and associated identifiers (such as MAC addresses) for each physical server to aid in future hardware maintenance. This is necessary because when HPE Helion OpenStack is installed on physical servers, the TripleO automation tracks only the MAC network addresses of servers; the physical locations of servers are not tracked. This means there is no automated way to inform a service technician which slot or rack to go to when service is needed on a particular physical server.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<othermeta name="product-version" content="HPE Helion Openstack 1.1"/>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<othermeta name="product-version1" content="HPE Helion Openstack 1.1"/>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>This document provides guidance on configuring your HPE Helion OpenStack network securely</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack has many built-in security controls, but the customer must take responsibility for configuring the network devices that integrate Helion services into an existing data center environment.  This includes defining firewall rules at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against external abuse) as well as defining router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors).</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is deployed on three physical networks: IPMI, Fibre Channel, and the Cloud LAN which is subdivided into VLANs to produce the External, Management, and Service LANs as depicted in <xref type="section" href="#topic20483/fig1">Figure 1</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<section id="fig1"> <title>Figure 1: Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>In <xref type="section" href="#topic20483/fig1">Figure 1</xref>, the Border Router and the Aggregation Router are customer devices that perform routing at the perimeter of the environment. The Load Balancer is a recommended customer device to provide TLS termination. The following sections provide guidance on how to configure these network devices for improved security.  Note that HPE Helion OpenStack includes IPtable rules on each node to close network ports that are not needed, but applying additional rules to your network devices (as indicated in the sections that follow) will provide increased security.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>As shown in figure <xref type="section" href="#topic20483/fig1">Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</xref>, all of the Cloud Controller servers are members of all three VLANs. However, these servers have IP addresses configured only for the management VLAN.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:              Helion OpenStack TLS Support</xref> HPE Helion OpenStack TLS Support</note></li>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>To protect against external attacks on Helion services, your firewall should be configured with a rule to block any requests originating from outside the network that attempts to reach any of the HPE Helion OpenStack nodes or any 3PAR StoreServ  or StoreVirtual VSA appliances dedicated to the HPE Helion OpenStack installation, other than those indicated this table:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>The customer deploying HPE Helion OpenStack is responsible for securing the block storage networks. Network data flows for block storage should be restricted using access control lists or other mechanisms in the customer's network devices which can include routers, switches, or firewalls. Block storage data flows interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack are described here to assist with defining those controls. References are given to documentation on data flows within the storage cluster itself, but not necessarily interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack nodes.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports StoreVirtual or 3Par StoreServ storage arrays which are described separately.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>HPE Helion Openstack supports iSCSI or Fibre Channel connectivity with 3PAR StoreServ. If using Fibre Channel, then the Compute nodes and the overcloud controller hosting Block Storage (Cinder) will require Fibre Channel connectivity with the 3PAR array. For iSCSI, connectivity will be through the management VLAN. The StoreServ REST API and SSH command line interfaces must be accessible from the management VLAN as well.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita:<p>If your deployment includes ESX Integration, you can improve network security by configuring access control lists for the ESX network.  The ESX Tenant network (also shown below) is managed by the Networking Operations service (Neutron).  The ESX network is not installed or managed by HPE Helion OpenStack You must install and manage this network and makes sure there is a route to the Management network.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-vsa.dita:<p>The license for the StoreVirtual VSA license is bundled with HPE Helion OpenStack and has a maximum limit of 50 TB per node. Hence the total amount of the configured storage on an individual StoreVirtual node should not exceed 50 TB. To extend the 50 TB per node limit, you can add nodes. A VSA cluster can support up to 16 nodes, which means configured storage on a VSA cluster can be as much as 800 TB.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-vsa.dita:**Note**: Use of StoreVirtual VSA is included with your HPE Helion OpenStack license. This message displays in error and can be ignored if you have licensed the physical server with a HPE Helion OpenStack license.

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>Thank you for your interest in HPE Helion OpenStack This document provides an overview of the features contained within HPE Helion OpenStack version 1.01, including known issues and workarounds, and where to find further information on the product release:</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="features"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack by release.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic19697/110">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic19697/101">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.01</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<xref type="section" href="#topic19697/10">HPE Helion OpenStack 1.0</xref>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="110"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:  <b>OpenStack Juno support</b> All of the <xref href="1.1commerical.services-overview.dita#topic8293/OpenStack" type="section">HPE Helion Openstack services</xref> have been updated to <xref href="http://www.openstack.org/software/juno/" scope="external" format="html">OpenStack Juno</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Metering services</b> The <xref href="1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita">HPE Helion OpenStack Telemetry and Reporting service</xref> leverages the OpenStack Ceilometer metering service. The Metering Operations service takes specified measurements of both physical and virtual resources, including physical servers and network devices such as switches and firewalls.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Windows Server validation as a guest O/S on KVM</b> - HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1 has achieved <xref href="http://www.windowsservercatalog.com/svvp/" scope="external" format="html">Microsoft Server Virtualization Validation Program</xref> (SVVP) approval.  As such, HPE Helion OpenStack is a validated and supported virtual environment for Windows Server 2012 R2, 2012, 2008 R2, and 2008.  <!--HPM-29--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>For information on creating and deploying a Microsoft Windows Server that is Microsoft SVVP compliant on HPE Helion OpenStack as a Nova compute VM, see <xref href="1.1commercial.create-deploy-certified-microsoft-windows-guest-image.dita">How to build a Microsoft Windows Server guest image for HPE Helion OpenStack</xref>.  <!--DOCS-917--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>New Horizon Dashboard functionality</b> - The <xref href="1.1commercial.install-GA-DNSaaS.dita">HPE Helion OpenStack DNSaaS service</xref> functionality is now accessible through the <xref href="1.1commerical.services-horizon-overview.dita">Horizon dashboard</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Transport Layer Security (TLS) support</b> - HPE Helion OpenStack now supports TLS protocols to protect internal traffic for Overcloud OpenStack API and endpoints. <!--HPM16--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Identity service</b> - The Identity service, based on OpenStack Keystone V2 or V3 provides one-stop authentication, including Identity, Token, Catalog and Policy services. See <xref href="1.1commerical.services-identity-overview.dita">Identity Service Overview</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:  <b>Compute Service Configuration Drive</b> - The HPE Helion OpenStack compute service can be configured to <xref href="1.1commerical.troubleshooting.compute.dita#topic6499/configdrive" type="section">write metadata to a special configuration drive</xref> that contains information normally available through the metadata service.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="101"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.01</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack 1.01:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Security documentation</b> - A new document is included in this release that contains recommendations for securing your HPE Helion OpenStack network. <xref href="1.1commercial.install-GA-security.dita">Configuring your network securely</xref> details the firewall rules you can apply at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against external abuse and defines router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</b> - The <xref href="1.1commerical.flexible-control-pane-overview.dita">HPE Helion OpenStack Flexible Control Plane</xref> introduces the capacity to deploy the control plane in a virtual environment in addition to the current baremetal physical deployment. This new configuration reduces the control plane footprint to just three servers from the current seven to ten servers.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<section id="10"> <title>Features in HPE Helion OpenStack 1.0</title>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<p>The following features have been added to HPE Helion OpenStack 1.0:</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>OpenStack Services</b> - The full set of standard <xref href="1.1commerical.services-overview.dita">OpenStack services</xref> is in HPE Helion Openstack Nova (Compute), Swift (Object Operations), Cinder (Volume Operations), Neutron (Networking Operations), Glance (Image OPerations), Keystone (Identity Management), Horizon (Helion dashboard), Heat (Orchestration), TripleO, and Ironic.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.release-notes.dita:<b>Support for VMWare ESX</b> - VMWare ESX is a baremetal hypervisor. HPE  Helion Openstack makes ESX host onboarding and management easier and lets you setup the ESX proxy node during installation of the overcloud.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.technical-overview.ga.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports VMWare ESX hypervisor. With our ESX integration, you can provision and manage an overcloud ESX cluster. VMWare vCenter Compute driver is used as a part of ESX integration. The VMware vCenter driver connects to ESX clusters in a vCenter through Compute proxy nodes. A Compute node scheduler sees each cluster as compute and uses the same for scheduling a new instances.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>OpenStack Juno support</b> <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->All of the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-overview.dita#OpenStack" type="section">HPE Helion Openstack services</xref> have been updated to <xref href="http://www.openstack.org/software/juno/" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack Juno</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Metering services</b> <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->The <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Telemetry and Reporting service</xref> leverages the OpenStack Ceilometer metering service. The Metering Operations service takes specified measurements of both physical and virtual resources, including physical servers and network devices such as switches and firewalls. The service employs filters to avoid high loads of inessential data on shared resources. <!--HPM24--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>Windows Validation as a Guest O/S on KVM</b> <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1 has achieved <xref href="http://www.windowsservercatalog.com/svvp/" scope="external" format="html" >Microsoft Server Virtualization Validation Program</xref> (SVVP) approval.  As such, HPE Helion OpenStack is a validated and supported virtual environment for Windows Server 2012 R2, 2012, 2008 R2, and 2008.  <!--HPM-29--> For information on the SVVP program, see Windows Server Catalog <xref href="http://www.windowsservercatalog.com/svvp/" scope="external" format="html" >Server Virtualization Validation Program</xref>.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<p>For information on creating and deploying a Microsoft Windows Server that is Microsoft SVVP compliant on HPE Helion OpenStack as a Nova compute VM, see <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.create-deploy-certified-microsoft-windows-guest-image.dita" >How to Build a Microsoft Windows Server Guest Image for HPE Helion OpenStack</xref>.  <!--DOCS-917--> Microsoft can provide technical support to customers with licensed Windows Server Operating Systems that are deployed as Nova compute VMs.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>Ceph Firefly Storage Solution Integration</b> <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.--> Ceph provides a unified, scalable and stable storage solution for the management of HPE Helion OpenStack Image service (Glance), Compute (Nova Boot Volumes) service, and Volume Storage (Cinder persistent Volumes) service. It also supports user backup and archive workloads to the Object (Swift) API service writing to the same unified Ceph storage platform. <!--hpm30--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:        <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->HPE Helion OpenStack now supports TLS
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>HPE Helion OpenStack Identity service</b> <!--A BR tag was used here in the original source.-->The Identity service, based on OpenStack Keystone V3 provides one-stop authentication, including Identity, Token, Catalog and Policy services. See <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-identity-overview.dita" >Identity Service Overview</xref>. While Keystone elements have been upgraded to v3, Keystone V2 is still supported.<!--hpm31--></p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.whatsnew.dita:<b>New Horizon Dashboard functionality</b> - The <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.install-GA-DNSaaS.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack DNSaaS service</xref> functionality is now accessible through the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-horizon-overview.dita" >Horizon dashboard</xref>.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.high-availability.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack Compute hypervisors do not support transparent high availability for user applications; as such, the project application provider is responsible for deploying their applications in a redundant and highly available manner, using multiple VMs spread appropriately across availability zones, routed through the load balancers and made highly available through clustering.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.high-availability.dita:<p>By design, HPE Helion OpenStack strives to create a system architecture resilient to SPOFs, and does not attempt to automatically protect the system against multiple cascading levels of failures; such cascading failures will result in an unpredictable state.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.high-availability.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack installer deploys highly available configurations of OpenStack cloud services, resilient against single points of failure.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-logging-overview.dita:<p>Because a typical HPE Helion OpenStack cloud consists of multiple servers, locating a specific log from a specific server can be difficult.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-logging-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack Centralized Logging feature collects logs on a central system, rather than leaving the logs scattered across the network. The administrator can use a single Kibana interface to view log information in charts, graphs, tables, histograms, and other forms.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-logging-overview.dita:<p>Centralized logging helps the administrator triage and troubleshoot the distributed HPE Helion OpenStack cloud deployment from a single location. The admin is not required to access the several remote servers (SSH) to view the individual log files.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack Metering service leverages the OpenStack Ceilometer service. A metering service takes specified measurements of both physical and virtual resources, including physical servers and network devices such as switches and firewalls. No matter what purpose the data is used for, this service provides a reliable, consistent method for data collection.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita:<p>The metering service is automatically installed as part of the HPE Helion OpenStack installation process. It may be necessary to install the command-line interface (<xref href="http://docs.openstack.org/user-guide/content/install_clients.html" scope="external" format="html" >CLI</xref>) separately to perform various administrative tasks.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita:<p>The initial default configuration enables a limited subset of all potential meters, collecting a few essential measurements from the Nova, Cinder, Glance, and Neutron services only. With these measurements, the Ceilometer API can begin collecting basic Helion OpenStack usage and status information.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-reporting-overview.dita:<p>Additional metrics collection for all of the HPE Helion OpenStack infrastructure services, as well as other application and platform services, are targeted for future Helion OpenStack releases.</p>

./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack Block Storage Volume Operations uses the OpenStack Cinder (Block Storage) service to manage storage volumes, including creating volumes, creating volume snapshots, and configuring volumes.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack uses StoreVirtual as a backend to Cinder to realize horizontally scalable block storage. StoreVirtual is unique in the sense that the storage controller runs as a virtual appliance and helps realize Software Defined Block Storage. To use StoreVirtual you must use the KVM hypervisor.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack also supports HPE StoreServ 3PAR as a Cinder backend.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>You can use the <xref href="../../commercial/GA1/1.1commercial.dashboard.how-works.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack Dashboard</xref> to work with the Volume Operations service.</p>
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:The following lists of tasks can be performed by a user or administrator through the [HPE Helion OpenStack Dashboard](/helion/openstack/1.1/dashboard/how-works/), the [API](http://developer.openstack.org/api-ref-blockstorage-v2.html) or [CLI](http://docs.openstack.org/cli-reference/content/cinderclient_commands.html).
./commercial/GA1/1.1commerical.services-volume-overview.dita:<p>For more general information on how to operate your cloud, refer to the <xref href="http://docs.openstack.org/ops/" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack Operations Guide</xref>. The <i>Architecture</i> section contains useful information about how an OpenStack Cloud is put together. However, the HPE Helion OpenStack takes care of these details for you. The <i>Operations</i> section contains information on how to manage the system.</p>

./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercia.ceph-high-availability-RADOSGW-authentication.dita:<p>Integrating the RADOS Gateway with the HPE Helion OpenStack identity service (Keystone) sets up the Gateway to authorize and accept Keystone users automatically. Users are created in RADOS pools provided they have valid Keystone token. ./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercia.ceph-high-availability-RADOSGW-authentication.dita:<p>Helion OpenStack 1.1 and 1.1.1 HAProxy can be used to enable high availability and load balancing for RADOS Gateway nodes. With HAProxy, Swift requests are load balanced between two gateway nodes. If one of them goes down, then all requests are processed by the remaining live node. Once the failed node recovers, load balancing is re-enabled. Load balancing is done using the round robin algorithm so that each node is used in turn, and load balancing is fair.</p>

./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>The HPE Helion OpenStack 1.1 and 1.1.1 Ceph Storage Solution provides an unified scaleable and stable storage solution for the management of HPE Helion OpenStack Image service (Glance), Compute (Nova Boot Volumes) service, and Volume Storage (Cinder persistent Volumes) service. The solution also supports user backup and archive workloads to the Object Storage (Swift) API service writing to the same unified Ceph storage platform.</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>This guide focuses on post installation, configuration and integration between HPE Helion OpenStack: 1.1 and 1.1.1 and Ceph Firefly 0.80.7 running on the hlinux kernel 3.14-29.4.</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>This guide assumes that you are familiar with the concepts of OpenStack and Ceph. ./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>Ceph is designed to deliver different types of storage interfaces to the end user in the same storage platform. The integration  of HPE Helion OpenStack and Ceph is the usage of <xref type="section" href="#topic7563/block-storage">block storage</xref> of Ceph's RADOS Block Device (RDB). Also, the integration between User Application Archive and Backup Workloads running externally or in Virtual Machines in HPE Helion OpenStack is the usage of <xref type="section" href="#topic7563/object-storage">object storage</xref> of the Ceph RADOS Gateway (RADOSGW).</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>The Ceph RADOSGW provides a REST interface with extensions which offers compatibility with the Swift API. Therefore the existing applications with the integration to the HPE Helion OpenStack Swift API can port seamlessly from a OpenStack Swift backend storage platform to the Ceph Solution.</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>The Ceph Block Device is a network-attached device, which is introduced to the HPE Helion OpenStack Controller and Compute Nodes for Glance, Nova and Cinder storage utilization, or, in order to meet unique SLAs, to the Virtual Machines in the KVM Helion OpenStack managed hypervisor. Glance can be configured with either Ceph object or block storage. Hence, HPE has followed Ceph's best practices and is limiting support for Glance storage of images to block storage. This allows for the support of Ceph's Clone and Copy on Write Feature (COW).</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:<p>The Ceph RADOSGW is a REST API which supports the Swift API. HPE Helion OpenStack supports object storage primarily for user workloads, ranging from COTS applications running in Virtual Machines (such as MySQL which frequently needs to archive tar files to a reliable and resilient archive) to custom LOB Solutions (which require frequent and aggressive snapshots orchestrated in a consistency group across many VMs and external baremetal systems).</p>
./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-overview.dita:to store data from Ceph block device clients or from Ceph file system clients. Ceph maintains its own user authentication and allows for extension to HPE Helion OpenStack Keystone Authentication. For User Archive and Backup workloads originating from HPE Helion OpenStack Tenant Project Virtual Machines, HPE recommends integrating through Keystone as a consistent authentication model.</p>

./commercial/GA1/ceph/1.1commercial.ceph-rados-gateway-dmz-ha-proxy.dita:<p>The Ceph storage system is successfully integrated with HPE Helion OpenStack Ceph has a RADOS gateway that is a public facing interface and is vulnerable. Hence, any end user can gain access into a Helion system with this integration. To minimize risks, an external HAProxy is built in a DMZ environment behind a firewall. HAProxy is commonly used as a load balancer for TCP- and HTTP-based applications. It works as a reverse-proxy, which means it maintains two connections when allowing a client to cross it: a connection between HAProxy and the client, and  another between HAProxy and the server.</p>

./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>This document provides guidance on configuring your HPE Helion OpenStack network securely.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack has many built-in security controls, but the customer must take responsibility for configuring the network devices that integrate Helion services into an existing data center environment. This includes defining firewall rules at the edge of the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against external abuse) as well as defining router rules within the HPE Helion OpenStack deployment (to protect against insider abuse or administrative errors).</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack is deployed on three physical networks: IPMI, Fibre Channel, and the Cloud LAN which is subdivided into VLANs to produce the External, Management, and Service LANs as depicted in the following figure.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<section id="fig1"> <title>Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</title>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>In the above figure, the Border Router and the Aggregation Router are customer devices that perform routing at the perimeter of the environment. The Load Balancer is a recommended customer device to provide TLS termination. The following sections provide guidance on how to configure these network devices for improved security. Note that HPE Helion OpenStack includes IPtable rules on each node to close network ports that are not needed, but applying additional rules to your network devices (as indicated in the sections that follow) will provide increased security.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>The perimeter is indicated by the Border Router icon in <xref type="section" href="#topic19956/fig1">Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</xref>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>As shown in figure <xref type="section" href="#topic19956/fig1">Typical HPE Helion OpenStack network topology</xref>, all of the Cloud Controller servers are members of all three VLANs. However, these servers have IP addresses configured only for the management VLAN.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>To protect against external attacks on Helion services, your firewall should be configured with a rule to block any requests originating from outside the network that attempts to reach any of the HPE Helion OpenStack nodes or any 3PAR StoreServ  or StoreVirtual VSA appliances dedicated to the HPE Helion OpenStack installation, other than those indicated this table:</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>The customer deploying HPE Helion OpenStack is responsible for securing the block storage networks. Network data flows for block storage should be restricted using access control lists or other mechanisms in the customer's network devices which can include routers, switches, or firewalls. Block storage data flows interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack are described here to assist with defining those controls. References are given to documentation on data flows within the storage cluster itself, but not necessarily interacting with HPE Helion OpenStack nodes.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack supports StoreVirtual or 3Par StoreServ storage arrays which are described separately.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>HPE Helion Openstack supports iSCSI or Fibre Channel connectivity with 3PAR StoreServ. If using Fibre Channel, then the Compute nodes and the overcloud controller hosting Block Storage (Cinder) will require Fibre Channel connectivity with the 3PAR array. For iSCSI, connectivity will be through the management VLAN. The StoreServ REST API and SSH command line interfaces must be accessible from the management VLAN as well.</p>
./commercial/GA1/neutron/1.1commercial_neutron-post-installation-configure-network.dita:<p>If your deployment includes ESX Integration, you can improve network security by configuring access control lists for the ESX network.  The ESX Tenant network (also shown below) is managed by the Networking Operations service (Neutron).  The ESX network is not installed or managed by HPE Helion OpenStack You must install and manage this network and makes sure there is a route to the Management network.</p>

./community/community.faq.dita:<section id="whatcommunity"> <title>What is HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition? And how does it tie into the overall HPE Helion portfolio?</title>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition is the first OpenStack distribution from HP. It is free to download and will be kept updated frequently to stay current with OpenStack developments. It will be a foundational technology for all HPE Helion products in the future.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>The final version of this free distribution will enable customers to evaluate HPE Helion OpenStack and to deploy small-scale private clouds in production (up to 30 nodes). They will be able to do this more quickly and easily with HP's simplified installation and update mechanisms.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<section id="howcompare"> <title>How does HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition compare to other OpenStack cloud distributions on the market?</title>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition is one of the first distributions in the market, based on up-to-date code from the OpenStack community. It is derived from pure OpenStack software and open source technologies, configured and packaged by HP. For example, TripleO, which is used for installation and update, is the official OpenStack project for deployment.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>It is free to download. An optional support package is available to purchase from HPE for access to HPE Helion OpenStack technical support.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>On May 7<sup>th</sup>, we announced a virtual preview of HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition that allows our customers to deploy an OpenStack cloud-in-a-box on a single physical machine. Customers are able to experience TripleO based deployment and to evaluate the Icehouse release of OpenStack cloud.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>On June 12<sup>th</sup>, we announced a GA version of HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition with support for baremetal installation, allowing the creation of OpenStack systems spanning up to 30 physical servers.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition will be updated frequently to keep pace with OpenStack platform  developments. We plan to release new versions roughly every six weeks, and to track the community development cycle.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<section id="hybridorpubliccloud"> <title>Will HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition work with hybrid or public cloud projects?</title>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition is API-compatible with HPE Helion Public Cloud, allowing workloads developed on one to be deployed on the other.  Compatibility with other Public Clouds will depend on which OpenStack platform features they chose to support. It is tested and supported by HPE for enterprise-grade, small-scale, private cloud deployments. Workloads are upgradeable to <xref href="../community/community.index.dita" >HPE Helion OpenStack</xref>, with features and capabilities needed for the enterprise, government, and service provider markets, to be launched later this calendar year.</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<section id="upgrade"> <title>Is the HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition upgradable?</title>
./community/community.faq.dita:<p>Yes. Customers who begin with HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition can migrate to larger, enterprise-grade installations using full HPE Helion OpenStack</p>
./community/community.faq.dita:<section id="nonhphardware"> <title>Can HPE Helion OpenStack Community edition be run on non-HPE hardware?</title>

The Community edition is a pure and free-to-license distribution that speeds deployment and simplifies the management of small scale open cloud environments and infrastructure services. It supports up to 30 physical nodes and 600 virtual nodes making it ideal for small-scale and proof of concept deployments.

./community/community.index.dita:<p>For information on how to operate and manage your cloud, we suggest you read the <xref href="http://docs.openstack.org/ops/" scope="external" format="html" >OpenStack Operations Guide</xref>. The <i>Architecture</i> section contains useful information about how an OpenStack Cloud is put together. However, the HPE Helion OpenStack Community takes care of these details for you!</p>
